The `ObligationForest` is a utility data structure used in trait\n     2→//! matching to track the set of outstanding obligations (those not yet\n     3→//! resolved to success or error). It also tracks the \"backtrace\" of each\n     4→//! pending obligation (why we are trying to figure this out in the first\n     5→//! place).\n     6→//!\n     7→//! ### External view\n     8→//!\n     9→//! `ObligationForest` supports two main public operations (there are a\n    10→//! few others not discussed here):\n    11→//!\n    12→//! 1. Add a new root obligations (`register_obligation`).\n    13→//! 2. Process the pending obligations (`process_obligations`).\n    14→//!\n    15→//! When a new obligation `N` is added, it becomes the root of an\n    16→//! obligation tree. This tree can also carry some per-tree state `T`,\n    17→//! which is given at the same time. This tree is a singleton to start, so\n    18→//! `N` is both the root and the only leaf. Each time the\n    19→//! `process_obligations` method is called, it will invoke its callback\n    20→//! with every pending obligation (so that will include `N`, the first\n    21→//! time). The callback also receives a (mutable) reference to the\n    22→//! per-tree state `T`. The callback should process the obligation `O`\n    23→//! that it is given and return a `ProcessResult`:\n    24→//!\n    25→//! - `Unchanged` -> ambiguous result. Obligation was neither a success\n    26→//!   nor a failure. It is assumed that further attempts to process the\n    27→//!   obligation will yield the same result unless something in the\n    28→//!   surrounding environment changes.\n    29→//! - `Changed(C)` - the obligation was *shallowly successful*. The\n    30→//!   vector `C` is a list of subobligations. The meaning of this is that\n    31→//!   `O` was successful on the assumption that all the obligations in `C`\n    32→//!   are also successful. Therefore, `O` is only considered a \"true\"\n    33→//!   success if `C` is empty. Otherwise, `O` is put into a suspended\n    34→//!   state and the obligations in `C` become the new pending\n    35→//!   obligations. They will be processed the next time you call\n    36→//!   `process_obligations`.\n    37→//! - `Error(E)` -> obligation failed with error `E`. We will collect this\n    38→//!   error and return it from `process_obligations`, along with the\n    39→//!   \"backtrace\" of obligations (that is, the list of obligations up to\n    40→//!   and including the root of the failed obligation). No further\n    41→//!   obligations from that same tree will be processed, since the tree is\n    42→//!   now considered to be in error.\n    43→//!\n    44→//! When the call to `process_obligations` completes, you get back an `Outcome`,\n    45→//! which includes two bits of information:\n    46→//!\n    47→//! - `completed`: a list of obligations where processing was fully\n    48→//!   completed without error (meaning that all transitive subobligations\n    49→//!   have also been completed). So, for example, if the callback from\n    50→//!   `process_obligations` returns `Changed(C)` for some obligation `O`,\n    51→//!   then `O` will be considered completed right away if `C` is the\n    52→//!   empty vector. Otherwise it will only be considered completed once\n    53→//!   all the obligations in `C` have been found completed.\n    54→//! - `errors`: a list of errors that occurred and associated backtraces\n    55→//!   at the time of error, which can be used to give context to the user.\n    56→//!\n    57→//! Upon completion, none of the existing obligations were *shallowly\n    58→//! successful* (that is, no callback returned `Changed(_)`). This implies that\n    59→//! all obligations were either errors or returned an ambiguous result.\n    60→//!\n    61→//! ### Implementation details\n    62→//!\n    63→//! For the most part, comments specific to the implementation are in the\n    64→//! code. This file only contains a very high-level overview. Basically,\n    65→//! the forest is stored in a vector. Each element of the vector is a node\n    66→//! in some tree. Each node in the vector has the index of its dependents,\n    67→//! including the first dependent which is known as the parent. It also\n    68→//! has a current state, described by `NodeState`. It also tracks the \"backtrace\" of each\n//! pending obligation (why we are trying to figure this out in the first\n//! place).\n//!\n//! ### External view\n//!\n//! `ObligationForest` supports two main public operations (there are a\n//! few others not discussed here):\n//!\n//! 1. When a new obligation `N` is added, it becomes the root of an\n//! obligation tree. This tree can also carry some per-tree state `T`,\n//! which is given at the same time. This tree is a singleton to start, so\n//! `N` is both the root and the only leaf. The callback also receives a (mutable) reference to the\n//! per-tree state `T`. It is assumed that further attempts to process the\n//!   obligation will yield the same result unless something in the\n//!   surrounding environment changes.\n//! - `Changed(C)` - the obligation was *shallowly successful*. The\n//!   vector `C` is a list of subobligations. The meaning of this is that\n//!   `O` was successful on the assumption that all the obligations in `C`\n//!   are also successful. We will collect this\n//!   error and return it from `process_obligations`, along with the\n//!   \"backtrace\" of obligations (that is, the list of obligations up to\n//!   and including the root of the failed obligation). No further\n//!   obligations from that same tree will be processed, since the tree is\n//!   now considered to be in error.\n//!\n//! When the call to `process_obligations` completes, you get back an `Outcome`,\n//! which includes two bits of information:\n//!\n//! - `completed`: a list of obligations where processing was fully\n//!   completed without error (meaning that all transitive subobligations\n//!   have also been completed). So, for example, if the callback from\n//!   `process_obligations` returns `Changed(C)` for some obligation `O`,\n//!   then `O` will be considered completed right away if `C` is the\n//!   empty vector. Otherwise it will only be considered completed once\n//!   all the obligations in `C` have been found completed.\n//! - `errors`: a list of errors that occurred and associated backtraces\n//!   at the time of error, which can be used to give context to the user.\n//!\n//! Candidate assembly.\n//!\n//! The selection process begins by examining all in-scope impls,\n//! caller obligations, and so forth and assembling a list of\n//! candidates. See the [rustc dev guide] for more details.\n//!\n//! [rustc dev guide]:https://rustc-dev-guide.rust-lang.org/traits/resolution.html#candidate-assembly\n\nuse std::ops::ControlFlow;\n\nuse hir::LangItem;\nuse hir::def_id::DefId;\nuse rustc_data_structures::fx::{FxHashSet, FxIndexSet};\nuse rustc_hir::{self as hir, CoroutineDesugaring, CoroutineKind};\nuse rustc_infer::traits::{Obligation, PolyTraitObligation, SelectionError};\nuse rustc_middle::ty::fast_reject::DeepRejectCtxt;\nuse rustc_middle::ty::{self, SizedTraitKind, Ty, TypeVisitableExt, TypingMode, elaborate};\nuse rustc_middle::{bug, span_bug};\nuse tracing::{debug, instrument, trace};\n\nuse super::SelectionCandidate::*;\nuse super::{SelectionCandidateSet, SelectionContext, TraitObligationStack};\nuse crate::traits::util;\n\nimpl<'cx, 'tcx> SelectionContext<'cx, 'tcx> {\n    #[instrument(skip(self, stack), level = \"debug\")]\n    pub(super) fn assemble_candidates<'o>(\n        &mut self,\n        stack: &TraitObligationStack<'o, 'tcx>,\n    ) -> Result<SelectionCandidateSet<'tcx>, SelectionError<'tcx>> {\n        let TraitObligationStack { obligation, .. } = *stack;\n        let obligation = &Obligation {\n            param_env: obligation.param_env,\n            cause: obligation.cause.clone(),\n            recursion_depth: obligation.recursion_depth,\n            predicate: self.infcx.resolve_vars_if_possible(obligation.predicate),\n        };\n\n        if obligation.predicate.skip_binder().self_ty().is_ty_var() {\n            debug!(ty = ?obligation.predicate.skip_binder().self_ty(), \"ambiguous inference var or opaque type\");\n            // Self is a type variable (e.g., `_: AsRef<str>`).\n            //\n            // This is somewhat problematic, as the current scheme can't really\n            // handle it turning to be a projection. This does end up as truly\n            // ambiguous in most cases anyway.\n            //\n            // Take the fast path out - this also improves\n            // performance by preventing assemble_candidates_from_impls from\n            // matching every impl for this trait.\n            return Ok(SelectionCandidateSet { vec: vec![], ambiguous: true });\n        }\n\n        let mut candidates = SelectionCandidateSet { vec: Vec::new(), ambiguous: false };\n\n        // Negative trait predicates have different rules than positive trait predicates.\n        if obligation.polarity() == ty::PredicatePolarity::Negative {\n            self.assemble_candidates_for_trait_alias(obligation, &mut candidates);\n            self.assemble_candidates_from_impls(obligation, &mut candidates);\n            self.assemble_candidates_from_caller_bounds(stack, &mut candidates)?;\n        } else {\n            self.assemble_candidates_for_trait_alias(obligation, &mut candidates);\n\n            // Other bounds. Consider both in-scope bounds from fn decl\n            // and applicable impls. There is a certain set of precedence rules here.\n            let def_id = obligation.predicate.def_id();\n            let tcx = self.tcx();\n\n            let lang_item = tcx.as_lang_item(def_id);\n            match lang_item {\n                Some(LangItem::Copy | LangItem::Clone | LangItem::TrivialClone) => {\n                    debug!(obligation_self_ty = ?obligation.predicate.skip_binder().self_ty());\n\n                    // User-defined copy impls are permitted, but only for\n                    // structs and enums.\n                    self.assemble_candidates_from_impls(obligation, &mut candidates);\n\n                    // For other types, we'll use the builtin rules.\n                    self.assemble_builtin_copy_clone_candidate(\n                        obligation.predicate.self_ty().skip_binder(),\n                        &mut candidates,\n                    );\n                }\n                Some(LangItem::DiscriminantKind) => {\n                    // `DiscriminantKind` is automatically implemented for every type.\n                    candidates.vec.push(BuiltinCandidate);\n                }\n                Some(LangItem::PointeeTrait) => {\n                    // `Pointee` is automatically implemented for every type.\n                    candidates.vec.push(BuiltinCandidate);\n                }\n                Some(LangItem::Sized) => {\n                    self.assemble_builtin_sized_candidate(\n                        obligation.predicate.self_ty().skip_binder(),\n                        &mut candidates,\n                        SizedTraitKind::Sized,\n                    );\n                }\n                Some(LangItem::MetaSized) => {\n                    self.assemble_builtin_sized_candidate(\n                        obligation.predicate.self_ty().skip_binder(),","numLines":100,"startLine":1,"totalLines":1441}}}

[rustc-dev-guide]: https://rustc-dev-guide.rust-lang.org/traits/resolution.html\n\nmod engine;\nmod project;\nmod structural_impls;\npub mod util;\n\nuse std::cmp;\nuse std::hash::{Hash, Hasher};\n\nuse hir::def_id::LocalDefId;\nuse rustc_hir as hir;\nuse rustc_macros::{TypeFoldable, TypeVisitable};\nuse rustc_middle::traits::query::NoSolution;\nuse rustc_middle::traits::solve::Certainty;\npub use rustc_middle::traits::*;\nuse rustc_middle::ty::{self, Ty, TyCtxt, Upcast};\nuse rustc_span::Span;\nuse thin_vec::ThinVec;\n\npub use self::engine::{FromSolverError, ScrubbedTraitError, TraitEngine};\npub(crate) use self::project::UndoLog;\npub use self::project::{\n    MismatchedProjectionTypes, Normalized, NormalizedTerm, ProjectionCache, ProjectionCacheEntry,\n    ProjectionCacheKey, ProjectionCacheStorage,\n};\nuse crate::infer::InferCtxt;\n\n/// An `Obligation` represents some trait reference (e.g., `i32: Eq`) for\n/// which the \"impl_source\" must be found. The process of finding an \"impl_source\" is\n/// called \"resolving\" the `Obligation`. This process consists of\n/// either identifying an `impl` (e.g., `impl Eq for i32`) that\n/// satisfies the obligation, or else finding a bound that is in\n/// scope. The eventual result is usually a `Selection` (defined below).\n#[derive(Clone, TypeFoldable, TypeVisitable)]\npub struct Obligation<'tcx, T> {\n    /// The reason we have to prove this thing.\n    /// FIXME: we shouldn't ignore the cause but instead change the affected visitors\n    /// to only visit predicates manually.\n    #[type_foldable(identity)]\n    #[type_visitable(ignore)]\n    pub cause: ObligationCause<'tcx>,\n\n    /// The environment in which we should prove this thing.\n    pub param_env: ty::ParamEnv<'tcx>,\n\n    /// The thing we are trying to prove.\n    pub predicate: T,\n\n    /// If we started proving this as a result of trying to prove\n    /// something else, track the total depth to ensure termination.\n    /// If this goes over a certain threshold, we abort compilation --\n    /// in such cases, we can not say whether or not the predicate\n    /// holds for certain. Stupid halting problem; such a drag.\n    #[type_foldable(identity)]\n    #[type_visitable(ignore)]\n    pub recursion_depth: usize,\n}\n\nimpl<'tcx, T: Copy> Obligation<'tcx, T> {\n    pub fn as_goal(&self) -> solve::Goal<'tcx, T> {\n        solve::Goal { param_env: self.param_env, predicate: self.predicate }\n    }\n}\n\nimpl<'tcx, T: PartialEq> PartialEq<Obligation<'tcx, T>> for Obligation<'tcx, T> {\n    #[inline]\n    fn eq(&self, other: &Obligation<'tcx, T>) -> bool {\n        // Ignore `cause` and `recursion_depth`. This is a small performance\n        // win for a few crates, and a huge performance win for the crate in\n        // https://github.com/rust-lang/rustc-perf/pull/1680, which greatly\n        // stresses the trait system.\n        self.param_env == other.param_env && self.predicate == other.predicate\n    }\n}\n\nimpl<T: Eq> Eq for Obligation<'_, T> {}\n\nimpl<T: Hash> Hash for Obligation<'_, T> {\n    fn hash<H: Hasher>(&self, state: &mut H) -> () {\n        // See the comment on `Obligation::eq`.\n        self.param_env.hash(state);\n        self.predicate.hash(state);\n    }\n}\n\npub type PredicateObligation<'tcx> = Obligation<'tcx, ty::Predicate<'tcx>>;\npub type TraitObligation<'tcx> = Obligation<'tcx, ty::TraitPredicate<'tcx>>;\npub type PolyTraitObligation<'tcx> = Obligation<'tcx, ty::PolyTraitPredicate<'tcx>>;\n\npub type PredicateObligations<'tcx> = ThinVec<PredicateObligation<'tcx>>;\n\nimpl<'tcx> PredicateObligation<'tcx> {\n    /// Flips the polarity of the inner predicate.\n    ///\n    /// Given `T: Trait` predicate it returns `T: !Trait` and given `T: !Trait` returns `T: Trait`.\n    pub fn flip_polarity(&self, tcx: TyCtxt<'tcx>) -> Option<PredicateObligation<'tcx>> {\n        Some(PredicateObligation {\n            cause: self.cause.clone(),\n            param_env: self.param_env,\n            predicate: self.predicate.flip_polarity(tcx)?,\n            recursion_depth: self.recursion_depth,\n        })\n    }\n}\n\nimpl<'tcx> PolyTraitObligation<'tcx> {\n    pub fn derived_cause(\n        &self,\n        variant: impl FnOnce(DerivedCause<'tcx>) -> ObligationCauseCode<'tcx>,\n    ) -> ObligationCause<'tcx> {\n        self.cause.clone().derived_cause(self.predicate, variant)\n    }\n}\n\n// `PredicateObligation` is used a lot. Make sure it doesn't unintentionally get bigger.\n#[cfg(target_pointer_width = \"64\")]\nrustc_data_structures::static_assert_size!(PredicateObligation<'_>, 48);\n\npub type Selection<'tcx> = ImplSource<'tcx, PredicateObligation<'tcx>>;\n\n/// A callback that can be provided to `inspect_typeck`. Invoked on evaluation\n/// of root obligations.\npub type ObligationInspector<'tcx> =\n    fn(&InferCtxt<'tcx>, &PredicateObligation<'tcx>, Result<Certainty, NoSolution>);\n\nimpl<'tcx, O> Obligation<'tcx, O> {\n    pub fn new(\n        tcx: TyCtxt<'tcx>,\n        cause: ObligationCause<'tcx>,\n        param_env: ty::ParamEnv<'tcx>,\n        predicate: impl Upcast<TyCtxt<'tcx>, O>,\n    ) -> Obligation<'tcx, O> {\n        Self::with_depth(tcx, cause, 0, param_env, predicate)\n    }\n\n    /// We often create nested obligations without setting the correct depth.\n    ///\n    /// To deal with this evaluate and fulfill explicitly update the depth\n    /// of nested obligations using this function.\n    pub fn set_depth_from_parent(&mut self, parent_depth: usize) {\n        self.recursion_depth = cmp::max(parent_depth + 1, self.recursion_depth);\n    }\n\n    pub fn with_depth(\n        tcx: TyCtxt<'tcx>,\n        cause: ObligationCause<'tcx>,\n        recursion_depth: usize,","numLines":150,"startLine":1,"totalLines":186}}}

fulfillment chain is a multi-stage process that resolves trait requirements and reports errors when obligations cannot be satisfied.\\n\\n## Obligation Forest (rustc_data_structures/src/obligation_forest/)\\nThe core data structure is `ObligationForest` (mod.rs:pub struct ObligationForest<O: ForestObligation>), which manages a forest of obligation trees. Each obligation can spawn child obligations, and the forest tracks the entire dependency graph. The `ForestObligation` trait (mod.rs:pub trait ForestObligation) provides the interface for obligations, requiring implementations to define a `CacheKey` for deduplication. The `ObligationProcessor` trait (mod.rs:pub trait ObligationProcessor) defines how obligations are processed with methods like `process_obligation` that return `ProcessResult` (Unchanged, Changed, or Error).\\n\\n## Fulfillment Context (rustc_trait_selection/src/traits/fulfill.rs)\\n`FulfillmentContext` (fulfill.rs:pub struct FulfillmentContext<'tcx, E: 'tcx>) is the main entry point for obligation fulfillment. It contains an `ObligationForest<PendingPredicateObligation<'tcx>>` and manages the overall fulfillment process. The `FulfillmentContext::select()` method (fulfill.rs:fn select) invokes `self.predicates.process_obligations()` with a `FulfillProcessor`. The `FulfillProcessor` (fulfill.rs:struct FulfillProcessor<'a, 'tcx>) implements `ObligationProcessor` and drives the selection process by calling `SelectionContext` methods.\\n\\n## Selection Context (rustc_trait_selection/src/traits/select/mod.rs)\\n`SelectionContext` (select/mod.rs:pub struct SelectionContext<'cx, 'tcx>) is the heart of trait selection. It maintains state like `intercrate_ambiguity_causes` and uses a `TypeFreshener` to manage placeholder types. The `select()` method (select/mod.rs:pub fn select) processes individual obligations using the following stages:\\n\\n1. **Obligation Preprocessing**: The `FulfillProcessor::process_obligation` method (fulfill.rs:fn process_obligation) resolves inference variables and handles type aliases before trait selection.\\n\\n2. **Candidate Assembly**: `assemble_candidates()` (candidate_assembly.rs:pub(super) fn assemble_candidates) collects potential implementations for a trait obligation. For trait trait obligations, it calls `assemble_candidates_from_impls()` (candidate_assembly.rs:fn assemble_candidates_from_impls), which iterates through all in-scope `impl` blocks and checks them for applicability. Other assembly methods handle specific cases like:\\n   - `assemble_candidates_from_caller_bounds()` - bounds from function context\\n   - `assemble_candidates_from_auto_impls()` - auto trait implementations\\n   - `assemble_builtin_sized_candidate()` - built-in Sized trait\\n   - `assemble_candidates_for_trait_alias()` - trait aliases\\n   - `assemble_closure_candidates()` - closure trait implementations\\n\\n3. **Impl Matching**: The `MatchAgainstFreshVars` struct (_match.rs:pub(crate) struct MatchAgainstFreshVars<'tcx>) implements a `TypeRelation` that matches a concrete type against impl types with fresh type variables. The `relate()` method (rg -A 5 for TypeRelation::relate) unifies types where one side can have fresh variables, determining if an impl could apply.\\n\\n4. **Candidate Confirmation**: `confirm_candidate()` (confirmation.rs:pub(super) fn confirm_candidate) takes the selected candidate and generates any nested obligations. Methods like:\\n   - `confirm_impl_candidate()` - confirms impl-based candidates\\n   - `confirm_builtin_candidate()` - confirms built-in traits\\n   - `confirm_closure_candidate()` - confirms closure trait implementations\\n   - `confirm_projection_candidate()` - confirms associated type bindings\\n\\n## Impl Coherence (rustc_trait_selection/src/traits/coherence.rs)\\nThe `overlapping_trait_impls()` function (coherence.rs:pub fn overlapping_trait_impls) checks for conflicting trait implementations. It uses `overlap()` (coherence.rs:fn overlap) to test if two impls could overlap, preventing incoherence. The function `equate_impl_headers()` (coherence.rs:fn equate_impl_headers) unifies impl type parameters to detect conflicts.\\n\\n## Error Reporting (rustc_trait_selection/src/error_reporting/traits/)\\nWhen an obligation cannot be satisfied, `report_selection_error()` (fulfillment_errors.rs:pub fn report_selection_error) creates a diagnostic. It matches on the `SelectionError` type (rustc_middle/src/traits/mod.rs:pub enum SelectionError<'tcx>), which can be `Unimplemented`, `OutputTypeParameterMismatch`, or `Overflow`. For unimplemented traits, it:\\n- Checks for similar existing implementations via `find_similar_impls()`\\n- Applies `OnUnimplementedNote` (on_unimplemented.rs) custom attributes\\n- Provides suggestions (suggestions.rs:pub fn get_explanation_based_on_obligation)\\n- Reports the error with context about what obligation failed\\n\\n## Core Types (rustc_infer/src/traits/mod.rs and rustc_middle/src/traits/mod.rs)\\n`Obligation<'tcx, T>` (rustc_infer/traits/mod.rs:pub struct Obligation<'tcx, T>) is a generic obligation with a `cause`, `param_env`, `predicate`, and `recursion_depth`. Type aliases include:\\n- `PredicateObligation<'tcx>` - obligation with a trait predicate\\n- `TraitObligation<'tcx>` - obligation with a trait reference\\n- `PolyTraitObligation<'tcx>` - obligation with quantified trait predicate\\n\\nThe `TraitEngine` trait (rustc_infer/traits/engine.rs:pub trait TraitEngine) provides the high-level interface for trait checking, with methods like `register_predicate_obligation()` and `select_all_or_error()`.\\n\\n## Summary of the Obligation Chain\\nThe process flows: `FulfillmentContext` → `ObligationForest.process_obligations()` → `FulfillProcessor.process_obligation()` → `SelectionContext.select()` → `assemble_candidates()` → `assemble_candidates_from_impls()` → `MatchAgainstFreshVars` matching → `confirm_candidate()` → error reporting via `report_selection_error()`. This creates a recursive system where confirming one obligation can spawn new sub-obligations that are added back to the forest, until all obligations are either satisfied, stalled (ambiguous), or reported as errors.\"\n}\n"},"caller":{"type":"direct"}}],"stop_reason":null,"stop_sequence":null,"usage":{"input_tokens":12,"cache_creation_input_tokens":2042,"cache_read_input_tokens":52313,"cache_creation":{"ephemeral_5m_input_tokens":0,"ephemeral_1h_input_tokens":2042},"output_tokens":1,"service_tier":"standard","inference_geo":"not_available"},"context_management":null},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"4df7cc34-686a-4755-9d5d-e747238e3fc9","uuid":"6192d02b-9c2d-44a6-bcbe-ab98f940c211"}

fulfillment chain is a multi-stage process that resolves trait requirements and reports errors when obligations cannot be satisfied.\\n\\n## Obligation Forest (rustc_data_structures/src/obligation_forest/)\\nThe core data structure is `ObligationForest` (mod.rs:pub struct ObligationForest<O: ForestObligation>), which manages a forest of obligation trees. Each obligation can spawn child obligations, and the forest tracks the entire dependency graph. The `ForestObligation` trait (mod.rs:pub trait ForestObligation) provides the interface for obligations, requiring implementations to define a `CacheKey` for deduplication. The `ObligationProcessor` trait (mod.rs:pub trait ObligationProcessor) defines how obligations are processed with methods like `process_obligation` that return `ProcessResult` (Unchanged, Changed, or Error).\\n\\n## Fulfillment Context (rustc_trait_selection/src/traits/fulfill.rs)\\n`FulfillmentContext` (fulfill.rs:pub struct FulfillmentContext<'tcx, E: 'tcx>) is the main entry point for obligation fulfillment. The `FulfillmentContext::select()` method (fulfill.rs:fn select) invokes `self.predicates.process_obligations()` with a `FulfillProcessor`. The `FulfillProcessor` (fulfill.rs:struct FulfillProcessor<'a, 'tcx>) implements `ObligationProcessor` and drives the selection process by calling `SelectionContext` methods.\\n\\n## Selection Context (rustc_trait_selection/src/traits/select/mod.rs)\\n`SelectionContext` (select/mod.rs:pub struct SelectionContext<'cx, 'tcx>) is the heart of trait selection. It maintains state like `intercrate_ambiguity_causes` and uses a `TypeFreshener` to manage placeholder types. The `select()` method (select/mod.rs:pub fn select) processes individual obligations using the following stages:\\n\\n1. **Obligation Preprocessing**: The `FulfillProcessor::process_obligation` method (fulfill.rs:fn process_obligation) resolves inference variables and handles type aliases before trait selection.\\n\\n2. **Candidate Assembly**: `assemble_candidates()` (candidate_assembly.rs:pub(super) fn assemble_candidates) collects potential implementations for a trait obligation. For trait trait obligations, it calls `assemble_candidates_from_impls()` (candidate_assembly.rs:fn assemble_candidates_from_impls), which iterates through all in-scope `impl` blocks and checks them for applicability. Other assembly methods handle specific cases like:\\n   - `assemble_candidates_from_caller_bounds()` - bounds from function context\\n   - `assemble_candidates_from_auto_impls()` - auto trait implementations\\n   - `assemble_builtin_sized_candidate()` - built-in Sized trait\\n   - `assemble_candidates_for_trait_alias()` - trait aliases\\n   - `assemble_closure_candidates()` - closure trait implementations\\n\\n3. **Impl Matching**: The `MatchAgainstFreshVars` struct (_match.rs:pub(crate) struct MatchAgainstFreshVars<'tcx>) implements a `TypeRelation` that matches a concrete type against impl types with fresh type variables. The `relate()` method (rg -A 5 for TypeRelation::relate) unifies types where one side can have fresh variables, determining if an impl could apply.\\n\\n4. **Candidate Confirmation**: `confirm_candidate()` (confirmation.rs:pub(super) fn confirm_candidate) takes the selected candidate and generates any nested obligations. Methods like:\\n   - `confirm_impl_candidate()` - confirms impl-based candidates\\n   - `confirm_builtin_candidate()` - confirms built-in traits\\n   - `confirm_closure_candidate()` - confirms closure trait implementations\\n   - `confirm_projection_candidate()` - confirms associated type bindings\\n\\n## Impl Coherence (rustc_trait_selection/src/traits/coherence.rs)\\nThe `overlapping_trait_impls()` function (coherence.rs:pub fn overlapping_trait_impls) checks for conflicting trait implementations. It uses `overlap()` (coherence.rs:fn overlap) to test if two impls could overlap, preventing incoherence. The function `equate_impl_headers()` (coherence.rs:fn equate_impl_headers) unifies impl type parameters to detect conflicts.\\n\\n## Error Reporting (rustc_trait_selection/src/error_reporting/traits/)\\nWhen an obligation cannot be satisfied, `report_selection_error()` (fulfillment_errors.rs:pub fn report_selection_error) creates a diagnostic. It matches on the `SelectionError` type (rustc_middle/src/traits/mod.rs:pub enum SelectionError<'tcx>), which can be `Unimplemented`, `OutputTypeParameterMismatch`, or `Overflow`. For unimplemented traits, it:\\n- Checks for similar existing implementations via `find_similar_impls()`\\n- Applies `OnUnimplementedNote` (on_unimplemented.rs) custom attributes\\n- Provides suggestions (suggestions.rs:pub fn get_explanation_based_on_obligation)\\n- Reports the error with context about what obligation failed\\n\\n## Core Types (rustc_infer/src/traits/mod.rs and rustc_middle/src/traits/mod.rs)\\n`Obligation<'tcx, T>` (rustc_infer/traits/mod.rs:pub struct Obligation<'tcx, T>) is a generic obligation with a `cause`, `param_env`, `predicate`, and `recursion_depth`. Type aliases include:\\n- `PredicateObligation<'tcx>` - obligation with a trait predicate\\n- `TraitObligation<'tcx>` - obligation with a trait reference\\n- `PolyTraitObligation<'tcx>` - obligation with quantified trait predicate\\n\\nThe `TraitEngine` trait (rustc_infer/traits/engine.rs:pub trait TraitEngine) provides the high-level interface for trait checking, with methods like `register_predicate_obligation()` and `select_all_or_error()`.\\n\\n## Summary of the Obligation Chain\\nThe process flows: `FulfillmentContext` → `ObligationForest.process_obligations()` → `FulfillProcessor.process_obligation()` → `SelectionContext.select()` → `assemble_candidates()` → `assemble_candidates_from_impls()` → `MatchAgainstFreshVars` matching → `confirm_candidate()` → error reporting via `report_selection_error()`.
